</span><span class="hl-identifier">#page-content</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-identifier">.table5</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-identifier">.scp-image-block</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-identifier">.scp-image-caption</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-brackets">{</span><span class="hl-code">
    </span><span class="hl-reserved">background-color:</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-var">#F5D8E0</span><span class="hl-code">;
</span><span class="hl-brackets">}</span><span class="hl-code">
 
</span><span class="hl-identifier">#page-content</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-identifier">.table6</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-identifier">tr</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-identifier">th</span><span class="hl-code">,
</span><span class="hl-identifier">#page-content</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-identifier">.table6</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-identifier">.scp-image-block</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-identifier">.scp-image-caption</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-brackets">{</span><span class="hl-code">
    </span><span class="hl-reserved">background-color:</span><span class="hl-code"> rgba(</span><span class="hl-number">146</span><span class="hl-code">, </span><span class="hl-number">0</span><span class="hl-code">, </span><span class="hl-number">255</span><span class="hl-code">, </span><span class="hl-number">0.2</span><span class="hl-code">)</span><span class="hl-code">;
</span><span class="hl-brackets">}</span><span class="hl-code">
 
</span><span class="hl-identifier">.tableb</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-identifier">.wiki-content-table</span><span class="hl-code"> </span><span class="hl-brackets">{</span><span class="hl-code">

</span><span class="hl-brackets">}</span><span class="hl-code">

    </span><span class="hl-reserved">box-sizing:</span><span class="hl-code"> border-box</span><span class="hl-code">;

    </span><span class="hl-reserved">box-sizing:</span><span class="hl-code"> border-box</span><span class="hl-code">;

<span style="color: black"><strong>Author:</strong> <span class="printuser avatarhover"><a href="http://www.wikidot.com/user:info/wynths" onclick="WIKIDOT.page.listeners.userInfo(9594206); return false;"><img alt="Wynths" class="small" src="https://www.wikidot.com/avatar.php?userid=9594206&amp;amp;size=small&amp;amp;timestamp=1777994449" style="background-image:url(https://www.wikidot.com/userkarma.php?u=9594206)"/></a><a href="http://www.wikidot.com/user:info/wynths" onclick="WIKIDOT.page.listeners.userInfo(9594206); return false;">Wynths</a></span></span><br/>

<span style="color: black"><strong>Total Word Count</strong>: <a href="https://tinyrituals.co/blogs/tiny-rituals/angel-number-12-meaning?srsltid=AfmBOoqL7cQRzMqWYmyNMZdPL8VIGVedwqSfLuEb608rcA2KYzjBW-UL" target="_blank">12</a><a href="https://www.astrology.com/numerology/angel-numbers/100-meaning" target="_blank">100</a> words (according to Google Docs)</span></p>

<div class="blockquote">
<div class="script">
<h3 id="toc0"><span>PROLOGUE.</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">1000 words.</span></p>
<h3 id="toc1"><span>INT. HOME. - BEFORE DAWN.</span></h3>
<p>The HOUSE-LIGHTS are off, but the audience can still the dim outline of the STAGE, expanding vertically to fit from floor to ceiling.</p>
<p>With a bang, they activate.</p>
<p>They are dim, rose red, and reveal three levels, stairs interconnecting them. The SPOTLIGHT focuses on the top-level bedroom. It is small, cozy. Two men sleep: Micheal, whom is 35, slightly tall, skinny, messy-haired, and Jake, whom is 30, stockier, darker, neatly cropped and shaven. Micheal snores loudly — a pill bottle lies open on his bedside table.</p>
<p>Jake winces. He opens his eyes after a beat, and sits up slightly. He rubs his eyes and, silently, leaves the bed. He sighs and looks at Micheal for a moment before putting on his clothes.<sup class="footnoteref"><a class="footnoteref" href="javascript:;" id="footnoteref-1" onclick="WIKIDOT.page.utils.scrollToReference('footnote-1')">1</a></sup></p>
<p>He goes to the second-level bathroom, and covers his eyes as he turns the light on. After acclimating, he washes his face, brushes his teeth, and stretches. He goes to the ground-floor kitchen, gets keys from a keyhook, and exits the home-model right.</p>
<p>The STAGE follows him, shifting the home-model left. He goes into a parking lot and yawns as he enters an battered truck with a ladder rack and toolchest in the back. He starts it after a failed attempt.</p>
<p>The curtain closes.</p>

<h3 id="toc2"><span>INT. OFFICE - WARM MORNING.</span></h3>
<p>The HOUSE-LIGHTS shine down from across a wall of glass. It has a red target painted onto it.</p>
<p>A row of blue private offices, facing the audience, are occupied. The gray-skinned workers wear the Foundation insignia. The center office is for Brandon—25, blonde, short, athletic build. He is on the phone and is mad as hell.</p>
<h1 id="toc3"><span>BRANDON</span></h1>
<p>What do you <em>mean</em> there was a mass-exoneration? That’s a couple dozen murderers they just let off the hook!</p>
<p>A pause. Brandon shakes his head.</p>
<h1 id="toc4"><span>BRANDON</span></h1>
<p>Insane. Can’t believe they let that slide through the system.</p>
<h1 id="toc5"><span>BRANDON (CONT’D)</span></h1>
<p>So what the hell does Command expect us to do? We’re not going to have enough D-Class for the explorations <em>and</em> Keter Duty! Do they really—</p>
<p>Brandon’s face grows stony.</p>
<h1 id="toc6"><span>Brandon</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc7"><span>(ICILY)</span></h1>
<p>Sir, I thought that policy’d been phased out.</p>
<p>A pause.</p>
<h1 id="toc8"><span>Brandon</span></h1>
<p>Well, I can arrange for that… are you confident? We’re understaffed as it is, sending a—</p>
<p>A pause.</p>
<h1 id="toc9"><span>Brandon (Reservedly)</span></h1>
<p>Alright, then. I'll arrange that, Sir.</p>
<p>Brandon pauses for a moment, nods, and hangs up the phone. He dials another number. He leans back in his chair, staring at the ceiling. It’s answered; he props his head up with his hands as he speaks.</p>
<h1 id="toc10"><span>BRANDON</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc11"><span>(WORRIED)</span></h1>
<p>Hey, Elena, execute Protocol Novena.</p>
<h1 id="toc12"><span>ELENA</span></h1>
<p>Novena? You sure?</p>
<h1 id="toc13"><span>BRANDON</span></h1>
<p>Yeah, ‘tis what Eliezer told me—we have no choice, the supermax we were contracted with bailed.</p>
<h1 id="toc14"><span>Elena</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc15"><span>(Irritated)</span></h1>
<p>God, what bastards! I’ll get the boys on that—anyone specific?</p>
<h1 id="toc16"><span>BRANDON</span></h1>
<p>Just the usual. Get some undocumenteds. Older, healthy people. Might do explorations with 'em.</p>
<h1 id="toc17"><span>Elena</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc18"><span>(CONTEMPTUOUSLY)</span></h1>
<p>Got it. Make sure you expunge me from this.</p>
<h1 id="toc19"><span>Brandon</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc20"><span>(Jokingly)</span></h1>
<p>I was on it already!</p>
<p>Brandon hangs up the phone. His smile vanishes. He resettles his spectacles, and begins typing on his laptop.</p>
<p>The curtains close.</p>

<h3 id="toc21"><span>EXT. HARDWARE STORE PARKING LOT - DAWN.</span></h3>
<p>Jake parks as the HOUSE-LIGHTS come on. They are warm but dim, like the light of early morning. The asphalt is cracked and white with erosion. There is a van and sportscar at the storefront. The windows are blacked out. The audience’s air is moist and smells of grass and exhaust.</p>
<p>Jake exits his car while on the phone. He waits at the front of his truck</p>
<h1 id="toc22"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Yeah, I’ll get the material, Garrison. Tell Bryan I’ll get his big sander too for the remodeling, but I had to go way out my way to get it. Feels like all the Home Depots are closed ‘round these parts.</p>
<p>Behind, another, larger van pulls in at the back.</p>
<h1 id="toc23"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>It’ll be done. Shelves ain’t that hard to arm, but I’ll tell you, this is one silent motherfucker. I already called them asking for approval, but they ain’t pick up.</p>
<p>Behind, a man built like a linebacker taps an earpiece. He nods and walks to Jake’s truck.</p>
<h1 id="toc24"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Was checking, that’s all! They’ll be done by the end of the day—just make sure it’s what they want, alright? I dunno if it is, and that worries me a bit.</p>
<p>The man adjusts his work-coat and checks his watch.</p>
<h1 id="toc25"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Alright. See ya’, <em>monstruo de la maza.</em></p>
<p>The man opens the store and flashes a look at Jake. He nods up. Jake puts his phone away and hangs his pocketknife from a belt loop. The man does not hesitate as he enters with Jake.</p>
<p>3 men exit from the truck’s cabins. They look at Jake’s truckbed and give a thumbs-down to the inside of the store.</p>
<p>A minute passes as these men wait against the door. A heated conversation is heard inside the store, though it’s unintelligible. One of the men cough. Jake leaves at that exact moment, and the doors slam into him, sending him to the floor.</p>
<p>The others burst into action, seizing Jake from both ends. He thrashes wildly, only barely contained.</p>
<h1 id="toc26"><span>JAKE (RAGGED)</span></h1>
<p>Help! Please! Someone, call—</p>
<p>He is silenced by the third man, who puts a mask over Jake’s entire face. Jake goes limp after a short struggle.</p>
<p>The larger van starts up and begins to exit the store. As it does, the third man unlocks the doors to the van and reveals a dingy interior, naught but a bench and sink. Jake is tossed inside, and two men enter the front.</p>
<p>The “storeowner” exits now, a bleeding cut across his forearm. He waves the first man over.</p>
<h1 id="toc27"><span>MTF-CAPTAIN</span></h1>
<p>You stay here, see how many more people show up.</p>
<h1 id="toc28"><span>MTF-MEMBER</span></h1>
<p>Yes sir!</p>
<h1 id="toc29"><span>MTF-CAPTAIN</span></h1>
<p>While you’re at it, check the guy we bagged. I’m positive he has nothing, but make damn sure. And flag anyone related to him, we'll amnesticize them later.</p>
<p>The MTF-member nods and removes a device from an unseen pocket. The Captain enters the sportscar and leaves.</p>
<h4 id="toc30"><span>END PROLOGUE.</span></h4>
</div>
</div>
<h1 id="toc31"><span>Pseudogenesis Productions Proudly Presents:</span></h1>
<p><span style="font-size:300%;"><em><span style="color: #fcca03">4012!</span></em></span></p>
<hr/>
<div class="blockquote">
<h3 id="toc32"><span>PREFACE.</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">333 words.</span><br/>
<em><a href="https://scp-wiki.wikidot.com/scp-4012">4012</a></em>, alternatively titled the David Lynch/LordStonefish Proposal, was a controversial novel published 3 months before the 1964 US-Presidential election. It criticized with contemporary clarity the direction in which America seemed to be heading: a future in which all humanity, mind and soul, was repressed through social and societal forces. While the author has revised it several times, the central premise has never changed.</p>
<p>To the non-anomalous public, the book is 300 pages of dream-like prose which depict a man amidst a sea of people with huge, monstrous jaws for heads: a fine premise, and one that is taken in directions unforeseeable by even the best critic. It is well-regarded for its incisive look into family relationships, the nature of forgiveness, and the subtle criticism of the homogeneity which America enforced on her citizens, which was brand-new in its day.</p>
<p>In the area of literary-anart, or litart, it is mostly praised and has won several awards, both for its use of dialogue-based memetic cues which were more seamless than anything its peers <em>could</em> offer, and the raw <em>power</em> behind each vivid image.</p>
<p>While the original revision of the book was already innovative, five revisions were published, each inching closer to the vaunted title of “revolutionary.” In 1995, this title may well have been achieved with what would be LordStonefish’s last return to the novel that started his career. That revision has the new title: “Teach Ten Thousand Stars How Not To Dance”, a reference to the infamous, striking image which closes the book.</p>
<p>This stage adaptation is a labor of love from all of us, most especially Stephanie and Vivienne. Whether we know it as Teach Ten Thousand Stars, 4012, or LordStonefish’s Proposal, we have all been deeply touched by this book and the impression that it made on us. Some of us even went into anart theatre as a result of reading this book.</p>
<p>We hope this does for you what it did for us.</p>
<p>~ Stephanie, Vivienne, Solomon, Duplo — The Pseudogenesis Crew.</p>
</div>

<div class="script">
<h3 id="toc33"><span>ACT ONE, SCENE ONE</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">800 words.</span></p>
<h3 id="toc34"><span>EXT. FOREST PATH. — DUSK.</span></h3>
<p>The HOUSE LIGHTS shine and illuminate the forest which surrounds the AUDIENCE. Both the lights and people sit comfortably on air. The forest is silent, sans a soft, opposite, breeze. A log CABIN sits a good distance away. Further is a lake.</p>
<p>The dusk splays orange across the sky.</p>
<h3 id="toc35"><span>MANIFEST — JAKE. 25, blonde, blue-eyed, disheveled prisoner.</span></h3>
<p>JAKE is manifested at the center of the stage. He walks along a path which stretches through the forest. He wears a black-blue earpiece that envelops his left ear, a light green jumpsuit with the Foundation insignia sewn on the back, and handcuffs. They clink loudly.</p>
<p>He is merely talking, but his words are amplified.</p>
<h1 id="toc36"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc37"><span>(AWESTRICKEN)</span></h1>
<p>Are all of the anomalies like this?</p>
<p>A COMMANDER responds to him through the earpiece. The voice is muffled and menacing.</p>
<h1 id="toc38"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>No, unfortunately. It just happens that this is a Safe one.</p>
<h1 id="toc39"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Oh.</p>
<h1 id="toc40"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc41"><span>(CHUCKLING)</span></h1>
<p>Yes, it's not all sunshine.</p>
<p>They continue in silence for a bit.</p>
<h1 id="toc42"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Is this all that there is?</p>
<h1 id="toc43"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>We don’t know that for certain.</p>
<h1 id="toc44"><span>COMMANDER (CONT'D)</span></h1>
<p>Keep walking forward or I’ll use that shocking device.<sup class="footnoteref"><a class="footnoteref" href="javascript:;" id="footnoteref-2" onclick="WIKIDOT.page.utils.scrollToReference('footnote-2')">2</a></sup></p>
<p>JAKE starts down the path.</p>
<h1 id="toc45"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>You still won't tell me what's at the end here?</p>
<p>He continues for a while.</p>
<h1 id="toc46"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc47"><span>(Worried)</span></h1>
<p>Why would you do all of this to investigate a cabin?</p>
<p>Silence, so thick it might attack you.</p>
<h1 id="toc48"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Answer me.</p>
<p>He stops a few feet from the CABIN. There is a dock there that was obscured by a shrub. It is short, well-maintained. At its end is a BOAT. It is windshorn and has patches of blue paint over a white hull. A name is embedded into it in red letters: “HOPE.”</p>
<p>A beat passes; the audience now sits some distance from the CABIN. They can see everything perfectly.</p>
<p>JAKE stands next to the CABIN's door, some feet away from the BOAT. He perks up.</p>
<h1 id="toc49"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc50"><span>(With confusion)</span></h1>
<p>Uh, what the fuck?</p>
<p>He leans against the door, remaining stoic.</p>
<h1 id="toc51"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Test connection, SALVADOR.</p>
<p>A metallic voice answers in monotone.</p>
<h1 id="toc52"><span>SALVADOR</span></h1>
<p>Connection: good condition. One hundred millisecond delay. Three-hundred and twenty kilobyte audio connection.</p>
<p>JAKE looks uneasy.</p>
<h1 id="toc53"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>COMMANDER, what the <em>hell</em> are you doing? Are you ignoring me?</p>
<p>JAKE waits a moment. The wind stops. He looks around. No one is in sight.</p>
<p>JAKE runs at full speed due west along the LAKE’s coast.</p>
<h1 id="toc54"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Oh my god… SALVADOR, condition of the COMMANDER.</p>
<h1 id="toc55"><span>SALVADOR</span></h1>
<p>Condition unknown.</p>
<h1 id="toc56"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc57"><span>(Hopefully)</span></h1>
<p>Please, please, please…</p>
<p>JAKE runs as fast and as far as he can, but the earth itself does as well. Trees swim through the ground like fish in water. The dirt kicks itself up, and JAKE closes his eyes to shield himself.</p>
<p>It takes a minute or two for him to realize he's trapped here.</p>
<h1 id="toc58"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Wait, wha…</p>
<p>JAKE bends, panting. JAKE looks to the horizon with their hand over their eyes, inspecting.</p>
<p>JAKE’s anger turns to fear.</p>
<h1 id="toc59"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Wait, no, wait, what the fuck… I was just—</p>
<p>The COMMANDER comes back.</p>
<h1 id="toc60"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>I see you’ve just arrived at the LAKE.</p>
<p>JAKE grabs at their earpiece. They wince at the subsequent shock.</p>
<h1 id="toc61"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>What’re you doing, trying to grab at the earpiece? You should know better than that.</p>
<h1 id="toc62"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Where?</p>
<p>The COMMANDER breathes, and does not reply for a moment.</p>
<h1 id="toc63"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>… The path. I've told you this 4 goddamn times. This will be your last command.</p>
<h1 id="toc64"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc65"><span>(Disbelievingly)</span></h1>
<p>Sir, there’s no land there! You said a minute ago—</p>
<h1 id="toc66"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc67"><span>(Forcefully)</span></h1>
<p>Did I stutter? Continue—we have not been able to acquire footage past this point. You'll be the first D-Class to transmit audiovisual information of 4012.</p>
<h1 id="toc68"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Uh…</p>
<p>JAKE walks to the BOAT. Its windshorn paint fades as he approaches. It turns white as baptismal robes.</p>
<h1 id="toc69"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>COMMANDER, do I use the BOAT to advance forward?</p>
<h1 id="toc70"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Yes. And do it quickly, my shift is going to end shortly. A new COMMANDER'll take over.</p>
<p>JAKE begins to untie the two iron chains which bound it to the dock. He manipulates them effortlessly, the chains folding in upon themselves to free the BOAT.</p>
<p>JAKE stops just before he releases the BOAT.</p>
<h1 id="toc71"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Who is this new COMMANDER?</p>
<h1 id="toc72"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>The name is COMMANDER, and they have a COMMANDER voice and a COMMANDER patience for discipline. I recommend you do not speak at all with the COMMANDER.</p>
<p>The words are chopped, clipped in their nature; JAKE does not acknowledge this.</p>
<h1 id="toc73"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Alright… COMMANDER, COMMANDER…</p>
<h1 id="toc74"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Are you going to take that step, DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE?</p>
<h1 id="toc75"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>What am I going to see out there, COMMANDER?</p>
<h1 id="toc76"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc77"><span>(Wistfully)</span></h1>
<p>Sunny skies and cloud-clear lines, DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE.</p>
<p>Wind whips through the theater. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE unties the BOAT, and the chain rattles. The BOAT drifts. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE jumps into it, stumbling and unsteady.</p>
<p>The HOUSE-LIGHTS dim.</p>
<h4 id="toc78"><span>END SCENE.</span></h4>
</div>

<div class="script">
<h3 id="toc79"><span>ACT ONE, SCENE TWO</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">800 words.</span><br/>
EXT. LAKE. - DARK DUSK.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE is hunched over, rowing the BOAT on a platinum lake with all its might. It knows it cannot stop rowing. Its face is contorted, its neck chiseled in the greatest effort. Its eyes are closed so that the sweat cannot enter them. Around it are a variety of flying things. It is close to the CABIN whence it came.</p>
<h1 id="toc80"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>COMMANDER, when will we get to that beautiful plastic place?</p>
<p>The COMMANDER remains silent.</p>
<h1 id="toc81"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Thank you, COMMANDER. I hope my work's good enough.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE screams, and the BOAT accelerates. There is no distinction between sweat and tears. The sound of shuffling comes from the earpiece. A few murmured voices leak through, but they are completely unintelligible.</p>
<h1 id="toc82"><span>SALVADOR</span></h1>
<p>D-112, you are currently… 75 meters from the opposite coast of the body of water. Keep going, you can do this!</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE almost stops rowing, trying and failing to take a slight break. Its skin runs red.</p>
<h1 id="toc83"><span>SALVADOR</span></h1>
<p>Motion has been detected. Disciplinary measures may be applied by your COMMANDER as seen fit.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE looks at the sky.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE takes off its earpiece and continues to row. It speaks to the air.</p>
<h1 id="toc84"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Are you there? Goddamn it.</p>
<p>The silence continues. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE becomes obviously upset at it.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE leans forward. It holds the earpiece to their mouth with one hand and passively moves the paddle with the other.</p>
<h1 id="toc85"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc86"><span>(LOUDLY)</span></h1>
<p>You coward! How long have you left me like this?</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE almost jumps forward with the power of its words.</p>
<p>A buzz is heard.</p>
<h1 id="toc87"><span>SALVADOR</span></h1>
<p>The connection between COMMANDER and DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE has been severed for 4 hours. Would you like to reestablish the connection?</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE wears the earpiece in reverse, cleaning and inserting it into their opposing ear.</p>
<h1 id="toc88"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>SALVADOR, I thought I told you not to ask me stupid questions.</p>
<h1 id="toc89"><span>SALVADOR</span></h1>
<p>Attempting to establish connection…</p>
<p>A moment passes, and a high tone is heard from the earpiece.</p>
<p>JAKE is surprised. They wipe their face and clean themselves as the COMMANDER speaks, the dulcet tones of her voice as sweet as though they were a COMMANDER’s.</p>
<p>And they are.</p>
<h1 id="toc90"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Wait… yes, yes!</p>
<h1 id="toc91"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>COMMANDER?</p>
<h1 id="toc92"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>My love, I cannot believe that it is you!</p>
<p>COMMANDER chuckles; a loving chuckle, just as a COMMANDER would.</p>
<h1 id="toc93"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>COMMANDER…</p>
<h1 id="toc94"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE…</p>
<h1 id="toc95"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Where have you been all this time?</p>
<h1 id="toc96"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>I've been trying to reach you. I wanted to help you, to give you silver and strength. But I couldn't find you 'till now.</p>
<h1 id="toc97"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc98"><span>(With a zen-like air)</span></h1>
<p>Thank you. I… I suppose that's what I should say.</p>
<h1 id="toc99"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc100"><span>(Gravely)</span></h1>
<p>I suppose too.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE leans backwards and puts their hands onto the paddles.</p>
<h1 id="toc101"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Oh, oh. Please—don’t touch that thing!</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE keeps touching the paddles.</p>
<h1 id="toc102"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>COMMANDER?</p>
<h1 id="toc103"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>My DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE, you mustn’t dabble with that. That is a dangerous thing to do.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE rows once. The BOAT moves three paces.</p>
<p>The COMMANDER shrieks.</p>
<h1 id="toc104"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc105"><span>(PANICKED)</span></h1>
<p>No! No, my DISPOSABLE, you can't do that — for <em>God's</em> sake! Do not do that again, please, my…</p>
<h1 id="toc106"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>COMMANDER?</p>
<h1 id="toc107"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc108"><span>(THANKFULLY)</span></h1>
<p>Oh… thank you. Thank you for listening. Stay with me. I'll save you.</p>
<h1 id="toc109"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>COMMANDER?</p>
<h1 id="toc110"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Please, my JAKE… what is it that troubles you?</p>
<h1 id="toc111"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>What if I don’t want to be saved?</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE’s COMMANDER gasps for a moment then reorients herself.</p>
<h1 id="toc112"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>What could you possibly-?</p>
<h1 id="toc113"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I think I need something more.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE looks around. Nothing but the flat lake surface.</p>
<h1 id="toc114"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>You have it with me, DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE. You have it with the story.</p>
<p>The voice is teary. Its words crumble together.</p>
<h1 id="toc115"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Thestoryneedsyou.</p>
<h1 id="toc116"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc117"><span>(REVERENTLY)</span></h1>
<p>And if something is beyond it? What then?</p>
<h1 id="toc118"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>ICANNOTGOBEYONDIT!DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVEICANNOTJOINYOUOUTSIDE.</p>
<h1 id="toc119"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I <em>don’t</em> think I’ll go outside…</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE begins to row. The BOAT speeds up, its velocity bleeding through the Upper and Lower Waters.</p>
<h1 id="toc120"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>ILOVEYOU.</p>
<p>The words are synthesized.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE rows for an interminable time. Soon, DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE hits the coast for which DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE aimed. The BOAT seems almost to tie itself as the BOAT slows, readying its next voyage.</p>
<h1 id="toc121"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>PLEASEICANNOTBEARTOSEEYOUGO.INEEDYOUMORETHANLIFENEEDSCARBON.INEEDYOUMORETHANTHESKYNEEDSITSCLOUDS.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE gets out of the BOAT with a jump. The audience follows.</p>
<h1 id="toc122"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>COMMANDER, I’m sorry. But I can’t stay with you forever. I need to live.</p>
<h1 id="toc123"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>OHGOD.OHGOD.ITHINKI’MGOINGTOVOMITIFISEEYOUGOOUTTHEREONYOUROWN.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE enters the second forest, the one unseen until you are at its shore.</p>
<h1 id="toc124"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>ICAN’TSEEYOUICAN’TSEEYOUICAN’TSEEYOU</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE whistles an old tune as it strolls through the path. Around it, trees are melting in the brilliant midday orange sun. It's a beautiful day.</p>
<h1 id="toc125"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>ICAN’TSEEYOUICAN’TSEEYOUICAN’TSEEYOU</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE interrupts its whistling and responds to the old hag.</p>
<h1 id="toc126"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>It’s okay, COMMANDER. I’m doing just fine out here! I promise, you don’t need to worry about me so much. What about Micheal—you should check on him, you know?</p>
<p>The COMMANDER screams. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE doesn't stray. The HOUSE LIGHTS dim.</p>
<h4 id="toc127"><span>END SCENE.</span></h4>
</div>

<div class="script">
<h3 id="toc128"><span>ACT ONE, SCENE THREE.</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">800 words.</span><br/>
EXT. FOREST PATH - ORANGE &amp; MIDDAY.</p>
<p>The audience sits in a real theater and in real, plush chairs now. They watch the play occur on a massive STAGE which stretches past their field of vision and into the horizon.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE walks down a path. Around it are hundreds of trees. Triangles are cut into their leaves. The antiseptic scent and the freshly-set plastic is overpowering.</p>
<p>Other paths are visible through small gaps in the foliage. There is a humanoid <em>Cymothoa exigua</em> and tardigrade. They are only visible for a moment, then they vanish into nothing.</p>
<p>Markings appear on the trees as DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE continues. They are meandering things, unknown in any tongue. They wander towards coherence as DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE ambulates.</p>
<p>As it continues walking, whistling to itself as it goes on, the forest begins gathering. Animals skitter about. A few birdgurgles are heard. It is serene.</p>
<p>The plaques begin displaying intelligible text. First, Pheonician. Then, Koine Greek. Latin. Etruscan. Franciscan Runes. Then: Old, and King’s, and modern English.</p>
<p>They describe the plants around them clinically, ascribing dead words to living things. The plants are not green, they display a presence of chlorophyll. The bark isn’t peeling, it is exposing the hard resin and silicone shell around the xylem and phylum.</p>
<h1 id="toc129"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Where are you? Can you—</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE removes its earpiece. It handles it for a moment, then puts it in its back pocket.</p>
<p>The birdsong is deep and pulsating, a massage to the ears.</p>
<p>There is another.</p>
<p>A shape comes from the distance, and DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE freezes. It leans towards a tree, then decides against it. It runs towards the shape.</p>
<p>As it gets closer, it notices that the shape is humanoid, and that it has stopped. It’s scared.</p>
<p>The two of it stop some distance apart, enough for each to see the other.</p>
<p>The shape was a skinless human—red, white, and striated—with the same dimensions as DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE. It wears a blue plaid shirt and an unbuttoned brown coat over it. The coat has a pen-pocket and shoulder pads stitched onto it. A large mouth with canine teeth and a long, slender tongue that flops about takes up its whole face. Its neck is pencil-thick and its trapezius and deltoids are pronounced.</p>
<p>It gulps, then emits a high-pitched whine that is more technological than biological. This is its mode of speech.</p>
<h1 id="toc130"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>What are you doing out here? Surely you’ve a place to go?</p>
<p>It screeches for a few seconds, wobbly in its pitch and volume.</p>
<h1 id="toc131"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>What? Why… why would you <em>do</em> that?</p>
<p>It clicks and screeches.</p>
<h1 id="toc132"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>That’s ridiculous. Look, I’m trying to go there myself.</p>
<p>It screams.</p>
<h1 id="toc133"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Yes I’m sure! Quite frankly, I’m not taking directions from some bitch yuppie like you. I’ve got quite the affair waiting for me, and I would not like to delay it a minute.</p>
<h1 id="toc134"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Hey… You wouldn’t mind if you gave me a couple pointers on its direction? I’m quite sure of where I should go, but I’d like to make sure.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE walks toward the MOUTH-ENTITY. It retracts its tongue into its mouth, and removes from its pen-pocket a pen.</p>
<p>It surveys for a bit, then rears back its head and shoots out its tongue at a nearby tree. It reels the tongue back, a piece of bark attached to it.</p>
<p>It envelops its thin, wiry nerves around the pen. It draws.</p>
<p>The map is crude but workable.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE lifts its head to the MOUTH-ENTITY, a small sign of thanks. The MOUTH-ENTITY replies with a gurgle, and starts walking again.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE continues down the path.</p>

<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE has put the earpiece back on. Around it, other MOUTH-ENTITIES fly and stumble through the foliage. If they fall, they do not get up. They are variously dressed, a deluge of normative representations. It is every character you have ever seen on the TV.</p>
<p>Some make silent cries. One stretches their tongue out, an apparent gesture of welcoming. None ever stop; they may be incapable of that.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE taps on the earpiece, and a connection is established. It is silent.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE comes nearly to the end of the path. In front of it, far on the backstage, is a grand gate, ringed at the top with 12 gemstones. Among them is jasper, chalcedony, and jacinth.</p>
<h1 id="toc135"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Why did you ignore us?</p>
<p>She is dejected, dead.</p>
<h1 id="toc136"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Don’t you—no. I don’t think you’re the boy I knew. Not anymore.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE leaves the forest behind it. For a moment, it pauses.</p>
<h1 id="toc137"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc138"><span>(GRATEFULLY, HOPEFULLY)</span></h1>
<p>You, you stopped. Please, keep doing that! You don’t need to go to those gates—you can still be saved!</p>
<h1 id="toc139"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I thought I told you a long time ago what I thought about that.</p>
<h1 id="toc140"><span>DISPOSABLE</span></h1>
<p>Please, no, don’t do this to yourself! You have a home with Mic—</p>
<p>The HOUSE slams shut.</p>
<h4 id="toc141"><span>END SCENE.</span></h4>
</div>

<div class="script">
<h3 id="toc142"><span>ACT ONE, SCENE FOUR</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">800 words.</span><br/>
EXT. WALL. - AFTERNOON.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE is at the gates to <span style="text-decoration: line-through;">his</span> dreams. Greenery abounds. Non-white sky. There is a toll collector's station next to it. Around it are various mouth-entities that wear straw hats and gardener's gloves.</p>
<h1 id="toc143"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>I cannot leave my seat now. I cannot, DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE removes a blank business card from its breast pocket. The mouth-entity standing in the booth opens its mouth twice.</p>
<h1 id="toc144"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I enjoyed talking to you too.</p>
<p>The gates swing open. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE enters, and what is beyond the barred gates is now visible. Its COMMANDER whimpers.</p>
<h1 id="toc145"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE, do you really hate me that much? Enough to do this to me?</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE retrieves a set of keys from its pockets, and opens the door of a black 2010 BMW X6 M.</p>
<h1 id="toc146"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Why.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE begins to drive. The STAGE seems to expand, taking it into itself. The <span style="text-decoration: line-through;">2010 BMW X6 M</span> BOAT goes 30, then 60, then 90.</p>
<p>It remains motionless.</p>
<h1 id="toc147"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>I remember when you were very little, DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE, you smiled.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE does not look back. It is responsible.</p>
<h1 id="toc148"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>It was a long time ago, wasn't it? I didn't feel like it was, but it went by so quicky. You learned to betray me so fucking fast.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE stops. It is at a crossroads. The left road goes upward, the right downward. Somehow, the audience is able to see both perspective clearly. The right leads off of the mountain. The left ascends into the heavens.</p>
<h1 id="toc149"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>You're going to do it again, aren't you?</p>
<h1 id="toc150"><span>COMMANDER (CONT'D)</span></h1>
<p>You always liked to follow me about<sup class="footnoteref"><a class="footnoteref" href="javascript:;" id="footnoteref-3" onclick="WIKIDOT.page.utils.scrollToReference('footnote-3')">3</a></sup>, and I got angry at it. I really did. But I don't think I ever did anything untoward, anything unfair. I… I don't know what to make of this. I don't know how I can get you to stop.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE restarts the BOAT. It shifts into the ninth gear, and the BOAT begins to climb. The STAGE shifts to accommodate DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE's vertical driving.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE and the BOAT show no signs of being affected by the 85-degree incline, and the BOAT progresses as normally as if it'd been driven on a flat road.</p>
<h1 id="toc151"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>You were always my little rebellious shit.</p>
<p>Stomachs lurch as the seating accelerates to move upwards with the BOAT. It climbs for a long while, and it never stops speeding up.</p>
<p>The shifting stops; DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE shoots past the STAGE.</p>

<p>EXT. ROAD.</p>
<p>It is at an intersection with a few others, an advanced form of the old dirt path. The MOUTH-ENTITIES look wildly about and drive perfectly. Some of them carry shadows in their cars, indiscernable at this distance. All you know is that they are child-sized.</p>
<h1 id="toc152"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>JAKE. Come back to me. You can still save yourself.</p>
<p>The COMMANDER breathes heavy, controlled breaths for a moment. She then disconnects the line.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE removes the ear piece due to lack of stimulus.</p>
<p>The line reconnects.</p>
<h1 id="toc153"><span>SALVADOR</span></h1>
<p>Connecting via Bluetooth to the BOAT. Please hold!</p>
<h1 id="toc154"><span>MICHEAL</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc155"><span>(RELIEVED)</span></h1>
<p>JAKE! Oh my god babe, are you alright? I, uh, I’ve been so <em>fucking</em> worried about you all this time! You just up-and-up-disappeared for god-knows-how-long and then these government-people came knockin’ at the door, and they were sayin’ that they’d-managed-to find you-their-coworker<sup class="footnoteref"><a class="footnoteref" href="javascript:;" id="footnoteref-4" onclick="WIKIDOT.page.utils.scrollToReference('footnote-4')">4</a></sup> but they needed some help from me? I don’t…</p>
<p>His stomach drops.</p>
<h1 id="toc156"><span>MICHEAL</span></h1>
<p>…Are you there?</p>
<p>JAKE decelerates. It is nearing <em>the</em> destination.</p>
<h1 id="toc157"><span>MICHEAL</span></h1>
<p>Are you driving right now? What’s, what’s happening?</p>
<p>JAKE stares forward.</p>
<h1 id="toc158"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Oh hey, Myke! I remember you from the game, man. How’ve you been?</p>
<p>Silence, for a moment.</p>
<h1 id="toc159"><span>MICHEAL</span></h1>
<p>Jake, what the fuck is going on? What game—no, you aren't even a sporthead, <em>I</em> was the one trying to get you to go to that Salvador game. You—</p>
<h1 id="toc160"><span>JAKE</span></h1>
<p>Yeah, that’s nice, man! Now, listen, I’m out here with this <em>really hot</em> chick, and she’s been telling me all night to go over to her place. She calls herself Sam. I was thinking, man, wouldn’t it be neat if you just let me crash at ‘er place for a second? She's in a good neighborhood, she's got some cute kids—bro, she's got a canal!</p>
<h1 id="toc161"><span>JAKE (CONT'D)</span></h1>
<p>It’d be neat…</p>
<p>Micheal walks away from the phone, the audience can hear him setting it down on the counter. The earpiece still transmits audio.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE begins driving home to her place.</p>
<h1 id="toc162"><span>MICHEAL</span></h1>
<p>[…] That’s not him! You’ve […] <em>wrong</em> guy, please <em>fucking</em> listen […] Best estimations. If it isn’t, then […] He’s not lost, is he? […] goes well. We <em>have</em> been able to put a location to him— —THEN WHY ARE YOU […] Soil, road conditions are horrible. […] Frankly, we don’t even know if it <em>is</em> […] GET YOUR FUCKING HANDS OFF ME! LET ME GO! YOU CAN’T LOCK ME UP IN MY FUCKING HOUSE!</p>
<p>And the line disconnects. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE exits and turns left.</p>
<h4 id="toc163"><span>END SCENE.</span></h4>
</div>
<hr/>
<div class="blockquote">
<h3 id="toc164"><span>FURTHER INFO:</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">333 words.</span><br/>
The revision we have adapted is the 1995 revision, the last one written by the original author. It was inspired by many subjects he studied later in life, with the works of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Julius_Wilson" target="_blank">William Julius Wilson</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technopoly#" target="_blank">Neil Postman’s Technopoly</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_G._Freedman#Works" target="_blank">Samuel G. Freedman’s Small Victories</a> playing a major role in his later work and making appearances in this last revision in the form of a more fleshed out father-son dynamic.</p>
<p>He became a heavy critic of what "the early Internet and media depictions of violence trended towards." Fueled by rage he felt at seeing coverage of the 1991-92 Gulf War on daytime television, he wrote several critically-acclaimed essays both on his personal website and in any newspaper that would print them, with the sole condition that the issues containing them be free.</p>
<p>He wanted to spread as far as possible his belief that America would lose its spirit to digital commodification and escapism. His initial theories of collectivization of thought by social pressure and widespread governmental propaganda seemed flawed, and he believed that the Internet and the culture it would bring would finally be the device with which human liberty was diminished.</p>
<p>Whether that has happened, is, of course, up to interpretation. He would cringe at social media and the rapidfire pace of thought now—he famously wrote a great deal on “intellectual bubblegum” and its detrimental effect on the collective attention span—but he might also praise corporations for having removed power over people from the government now, not realizing that his training to be skeptical of legal organizations would now have to be liberally applied to corporate entities.</p>
<p>Whatever he would think of the situation now, we can all agree on one thing; it is a goddamned shame that he is not around to give us more of his thoughts on the matter. The closest thing we have now is from 1995. That is why we have adapted that revision—it is the closest thing we have to a relevant <em>and</em> recognizable LordStonefish book.</p>
</div>
<hr/>
<div class="script">
<h3 id="toc165"><span>ACT TWO, SCENE ONE</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">800 words.</span><br/>
INT. HOUSE.</p>
<p>A wife-entity awaits DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE remains stoic as it's hugged by her.</p>
<p>The COMMANDER's breathing staggers. She barely avoids vomiting.</p>
<p>To DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE's front is a standard American High-Ceiling living room. It stretches fifteen feet above DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE's head.</p>
<p>A rug is at its center, and the rug is ringed with blue couches. A very small mouth-entity lays on the rug, bouncing a Walmart-branded ball. A teenaged mouth entity sits on the couch, and holds up its hand as DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE walks in. There is no acknowledgement.</p>
<p>War is on the flatscreen, stage left.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE sits next to the teenaged mouth entity, and eagerly watches the images on the screen. An older mouth-entity, still oozing juice, stands in a flat desert, and great black shapes loom in the sky.</p>
<p>The SON-ENTITY screams at his father.</p>
<h1 id="toc166"><span>SON-ENTITY</span></h1>
<p>Yeah… look at that one, I guess they’re pretty cool, ain’t they?</p>
<h1 id="toc167"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I always thought that they were magnificent too. Look at how big that one is! How many bombs do you think go in that one?</p>
<p>The SON-ENTITY screams at his father.</p>
<h1 id="toc168"><span>SON-ENTITY</span></h1>
<p>Not that many, hopefully. I’d say 10.</p>
<h1 id="toc169"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Maybe. I think it’s more than that. I think they’ll never run out, not if they’re from <em>this</em> country.</p>
<h1 id="toc170"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc171"><span>(DESPAIRING)</span></h1>
<p>I thought you were better than this, love.</p>
<p>The SON-ENTITY screams at DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE. Rage flashes on its face. It swallows and continues in a quiet, rough voice.</p>
<h1 id="toc172"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Shut the fuck up, you goddamned pussy—don’t think that simply because you’ve grown you can backtalk me now. Just enjoy it.</p>
<p>The teenage mouth entity stands down and sits barely on the couch. It is disinterested in the war footage; this goes unnoticed.</p>
<p>The wife-entity comes behind DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE. The COMMANDER is unsteady, but breaths consciously and irregularly. She is trying.</p>
<h1 id="toc173"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Please. Don’t let her touch you. My love, are you still in there?<sup class="footnoteref"><a class="footnoteref" href="javascript:;" id="footnoteref-5" onclick="WIKIDOT.page.utils.scrollToReference('footnote-5')">5</a></sup></p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE does not so much as depress its shoulders as the wife-entity begins massaging it, high-pitched gurgling coming from her mouth as it lingers closely to its ear. She rubs her chest against <span style="text-decoration: line-through;">his</span> neck, a bulge growing under the dress.</p>
<h1 id="toc174"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Tonight, my dear. Tonight.</p>
<p>The wife-entity disengage and leans at the side of the stage, waiting.</p>
<p>Suddenly, the SON-ENTITY goes into a frenzy of bouncing and chirping—an aerial shot of a town is on the screen! DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE smiles. The television expands. The wife-entity exits stage left.</p>
<h1 id="toc175"><span>SON-ENTITY</span></h1>
<p><span style="text-decoration: line-through;">No!</span></p>
<h1 id="toc176"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>No!</p>
<h1 id="toc177"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Come on… I know my men can do it…</p>
<p>A shape like the ones before swoops over the town. It drops a small black pellet which stops just above the ground and cardboard roofs of the pastel-tinted box-homes.</p>
<h1 id="toc178"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc179"><span>(EXCITEDLY)</span></h1>
<p>Yes! Yes! Yes! <em>The tech worked!</em></p>
<p>Many little streams of red exit the pellet, and they seek out people in the streets, latching onto their forearms, their thighs, their spine’s base, their eyes. People run out of their homes. Peoples’ skin greys and bones slough as the blood is sucked directly out of their bodies.</p>
<p>The SON-ENTITY claps once as the trails retract into the bomb, and then, in a great show, it explodes—the explosion is a maroon blip that lasts less than two seconds. It is small, pathetic, and efficient. A smile tugs at DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE’s cheeks</p>
<p>On the TV, the buildings break. There is no more evidence the desert was ever populated.</p>
<p>The baby bounces the Walmart ball, glimpsing at the screen as it contracts back to its normal position. It coos.</p>
<h1 id="toc180"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I told you, you simply needed to wait for the big moment! I’m sure that you understand now, yes?</p>
<p>The SON-ENTITY assents.</p>
<h1 id="toc181"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Good.</p>
<p>A bell rings. Dinner is ready. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE picks the baby up from the puddle of fluids on the rug, and the three of them exit stage left.</p>

<p>The wife-entity leaves the kitchenette into the dining room with a pot of boiling porridge. It is composed of writhing white worms.<br/>
A few of them get onto the table, their slime leaving imprints on it. The baby picks them off with her tongue, and the SON-ENTITY picks them into his plate.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE does not eat.</p>
<h1 id="toc182"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>You know you shouldn’t be here. Please, you need to wake up. My DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE, you <em>need</em> to wake up!</p>
<p>The rest eat in silence. They are voracious.</p>
<h1 id="toc183"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Don’t. Please, don’t.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE stands and goes into the kitchenette. It staches its bowl in the fridge and wordlessly exits stage right. The teenaged-mouth-entity clicks. The wife-entity does not respond. He puts two empty plates in the sink, raises the baby, and exits stage left.</p>
<p>The wife-entity dumps her plate into the sink. She grabs a bottle from a medicine cabinet and takes three tablets in rapid succession. She stumbles, grabs the counter, then reorients herself. She limps as she exits stage right.</p>
<h4 id="toc184"><span>END SCENE.</span></h4>
</div>

<div class="script">
<h3 id="toc185"><span>ACT TWO, SCENE TWO</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:75%;">800 words</span></p>
<h3 id="toc186"><span>EXT. PARK. — CLEAR NOON.</span></h3>
<p>The STAGE is covered in a luscious, impossibly well-trimmed grass, and the back has been given to the trees. Centerstage is a simple pavilion. Blackened wood are the support beams, and chewed mud is its glue. The sun shines clearly around it, making the grass almost yellow. A soft eastern wind cuts through both the STAGE and the audience, but the plants don’t move.</p>
<p>Under the pavilion are barely distinguishable MOUTH-ENTITIES wearing suits and DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE. He sits at one of the benches strewn under the shade. A suited mouth-entity cooks hamburgers on the grill and sets them into a plate; the rest of the MOUTH-ENTITIES dine over a substance similar to the wife-entity’s porridge, stored in large KFC chicken buckets.. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE and his partner are audible over the din of muttering and slobbering.</p>
<h1 id="toc187"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc188"><span>(DREAMILY)</span></h1>
<p>You know, I’m glad to be back here.</p>
<h1 id="toc189"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Parameters unclear; gratitude?</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE lets out a hearty chuckle.</p>
<h1 id="toc190"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Yes, I wouldn’t believe it either, but it seems like that decision has been rewarded tenfold. Consider: I would have <em>never</em> healed myself as fast as I did without it.</p>
<p>The PARTNER cocks his head and then goes on eating.</p>
<h1 id="toc191"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Oh, I know I would have eventually gotten back into the world of business, but it helps to be expedited, you know? With family, I’m not punished much for… <em>ignoring</em> whatever, but with you…</p>
<h1 id="toc192"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Goodwise understood, Twelve; half of family are deaf.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE nods wisely. PARTNER grabs a mouthful of worms from the KFC bucket and goes on.</p>
<h1 id="toc193"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Upthink! Downchance that you are negatived. Chance you are negatived? Go to real family.</p>
<h1 id="toc194"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc195"><span>(Slowly)</span></h1>
<p>It’s always an option, isn’t it?</p>
<h1 id="toc196"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Closedthinkers unlear-ned are uncapable of goodsortwise protest.</p>
<h1 id="toc197"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>But I don’t know! Are they truly unsalvageable?</p>
<h1 id="toc198"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>(KNIFEFUL)<br/>
No.</p>
<h1 id="toc199"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>You have to wonder though, don’t you?</p>
<h1 id="toc200"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc201"><span>(ANTEHATE)</span></h1>
<p>Yes. We can, will, see.</p>
<h1 id="toc202"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Hey, at least I managed to tune in, didn’t I?</p>
<p>They both snicker at the remark. The PARTNER nods and wipes his tongue over his face.</p>
<h1 id="toc203"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Plusyes: little ability to allful understand exists.</p>
<h1 id="toc204"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I know, I know, And it was… <em>so hard</em>, friend, it really was.</p>
<h1 id="toc205"><span>PARTNER (CONFUSED)</span></h1>
<p>Hearing?</p>
<h1 id="toc206"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Yes! You must have had some difficulties trying to listen in the past, haven’t you?</p>
<h1 id="toc207"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Unagree.</p>
<h1 id="toc208"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE (CONTEMPLATIVE)</span></h1>
<p>Huh… Really?</p>
<p>They are silent for a while. PARTNER goes to grab another KFC worm bucket, and he throws food into his maw as DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE beats rhythmically on the table and looks to the back.</p>
<h1 id="toc209"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>You know, you can tell me if you <em>have</em> had that issue before, right? I, uhm, I’m sure you can agree.</p>
<h1 id="toc210"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Confession: I have no family.</p>
<h1 id="toc211"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I see.</p>
<h1 id="toc212"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE (CONT’D)</span></h1>
<p>Uhm… I should count my blessings, shouldn’t I?</p>
<h1 id="toc213"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Recommended!</p>
<p>A pause. Some of the suited MOUTH-ENTITIES rise, salute to the west, and stack their KFC buckets on the floor by the grill. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE bows its head over the table and almost immediately sits back up.</p>
<h1 id="toc214"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I’m quite bad at it.</p>
<h1 id="toc215"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Reattempt?</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE rises from the bench and looks to the audience.</p>
<h1 id="toc216"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I don’t know if that would be of any real use. I… I admit, I don’t think counting my blessings has done anything for me.</p>
<p>PARTNER shrinks back, clearly surprised.</p>
<h1 id="toc217"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Elaborate?</p>
<p>It hesitates for a second, then continues—reinvigorated, anxious to explain and persuade.</p>
<h1 id="toc218"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Well, do you know how it is when you come to the house and you have a bitch of a son, and your wife has to pop the pills, and you pass up the canal?</p>
<p>PARTNER nods.</p>
<h1 id="toc219"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE (CONT’D)</span></h1>
<p>If you don’t know, friend, that feeling's surely anger. That is surely anger. It’s not bad, I’m not convinced of that, but it is there and it would like to take over—doesn’t it like to consume homes of wood, PARTNER?</p>
<p>PARTNER nods.</p>
<h1 id="toc220"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE (CONT’D)</span></h1>
<p>It can’t be their fault that I am mute and deaf, that much is certain. But can I know that they are truly okay?</p>
<h1 id="toc221"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Doubleplussurewise!</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE shakes its head and paces in frustration. PARTNER follows it.</p>
<h1 id="toc222"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>There is but one solution, one thing which compensates for my difficulty and hardness of heart. And I pray that it works, though I am mute for God.</p>
<h1 id="toc223"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Answer?</p>
<h1 id="toc224"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc225"><span>(DETERMINED)</span></h1>
<p>I <em>will</em> rise! I tell you, PARTNER, this little retreat is not enough! I need to… learn, I need to acclimate to the speech and the sounds and the burning smell of iron and plasma.</p>
<h1 id="toc226"><span>PARTNER</span></h1>
<p>Curious.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE straightens its shirt with a deft motion and pats its pockets. PARTNER waits.</p>
<h1 id="toc227"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I will serve my people.</p>
<p>The wind dies down. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE is the last person remaining in the shade. It steps out slowly. It looks to the sky.</p>
<h4 id="toc228"><span>END SCENE.</span></h4>
</div>

<div class="script">
<h3 id="toc229"><span>ACT TWO, SCENE THREE</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">800 words.</span><br/>
INT. OFFICE - COLD MORNING.</p>
<p>The audience looks down upon a great expanse from the comfort of lush recliners.</p>
<p>In all directions, stretching out to the horizon, is an open-floor-plan corporate office. Thousands of computers sit unused at the rows of dusty plastic fold-out tables which stretch beyond the audience’s view. A beanbag in the corner has three or four MOUTH-ENTITIES on it.. Footfall on the tile floor comes from everywhere—no one is visible on the STAGE.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE comes into the office from an elevator at the left side. The walls of the elevator are untaped sheetrock, the bare edges stained yellow with age and the splotches of plaster covering the nails unsanded.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE walks to a cubicle near a watercooler which has several MOUTH-ENTITES in attire similar to the PARTNER’s.</p>
<p>These MOUTH-ENTITIES approach it as it walks. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE snaps its head and pays attention.</p>
<h1 id="toc230"><span>MOUTH-ENTITIES</span></h1>
<p>ARE YOU EXCELLENT WITHIN YOUR ALLOTTED HOME YES I DO BELIEVE YOU ARE AND I APPRECIATE THIS VERY MUCH NOW WE MUST BEGIN TO WORK FOR WHAT YOU HAVE BEEN GIVEN OR YOU WILL BE.</p>
<p>A cart manifests, and the MOUTH-ENTITIES unfurl the chart within said cart to demonstrate. Its text seems to pop out, literally. On the chart is scrawled the words “TERMINATE RED MAXIMIZE GREEN.”, and a pie chart that is exactly half-red. A bar graph shows a linear downward trend.</p>
<h1 id="toc231"><span>MOUTH-ENTITIES</span></h1>
<p>ENSURE TOTAL ANNIHILATION AND REMEMBER ALL THAT IS NECCESSARY IS AND YOU ARE AT OUR BEHEST AND TOTALLY GIVEN PERMISSION TO DO ALL THAT IS REMEMBERED AND REQUIRED. CONDEMN. EXPONENTIATE THIS COMMAND.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE nods. It wouldn't let down its boys on the desert front even if it wanted to.</p>
<h1 id="toc232"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Please, DISPOSABLE, <em>even</em> if you don’t want to listen to me, you know this is wrong! This is not what a patriot would do, trust-</p>
<h1 id="toc233"><span>MOUTH-ENTITIES</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc234"><span>(THERE IS A TONE THAT IS INCOMPREHENSIBLE TO HUMAN EARS.)</span></h1>
<p>GO YES FORTH YOU WILL EXECUTE VERY WELL INDEED.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE removes the earpiece and places it gently upon the table. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE gets up from its chair and begins walking down the aisle with the MOUTH-ENTITIES, its impeccable suit ready for the grand day that shall come.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE grabs a standard-issue, military-grade, vacuum-packed, antiseptic, exsanguinated stamp from its stand and returns to its cubicle.</p>
<p>A stack of papers manifests itself on the desk as DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE sits in the plastic fold-out chair.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE begins to sort. It stamps and separates some plastic papers. The other sets of paper are either black or white. Black papers are thrown into a stack on the floor. White papers remain on the desk.</p>
<p>This occurs at normal speed for a few seconds.</p>
<p>With a cracking sound, the speed of what occurs on the STAGE begins to increase. Those sounds are heard every few seconds as the speed of the actors doubles.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE quickly becomes an illegible blur vaguely centered in the chair, and fleshy red-and-grey-and-skin lines are traced by the MOUTH-ENTITIES that walk through the aisles. Something like a calendar is shot out of the top of the cubicle and lands behind the elevator.</p>
<p>Vision constricts. Pupils dilate. The young in the audience feel their hearts beat a slow, irregular rhythm. <em><strong>WE</strong></em> rise.</p>
<p>90 seconds pass. The work is complete, and you are dropped back into your seat. All of the lights turn off.</p>

<p>Nothing has changed, but all has shifted.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE was disheveled; they are now undone. The suit has a ketchup stain on it. The low haircut is now a curly thing, with bangs and hair that spills over its ears. The black paper is ash, with streaks of red running through the whole mass. The white papers remain unmarked and exactly where they were.</p>
<p>The glass windows are obscured by darkness, and the target has vanished from where it should have been. The only HOUSE LIGHT active on the stage is trained on DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE rises from its seat and remains itself as it walk through the aisle. It goes to the elevator; a phone has been installed. The dust is still unswept on the ground.</p>
<p>It uses it.</p>
<p>It rings.</p>
<p>And someone familiar at the end of the line picks up.</p>
<h1 id="toc235"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Son?</p>
<h1 id="toc236"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Fuck, yes… I know. How long <em>has</em> it been?</p>
<h1 id="toc237"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>No. It couldn’t have been.</p>
<h1 id="toc238"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I remember you when you were so little you couldn’t even hold up the logs that I tried to buy from the Home Depot. It was for that little project, remember? We wanted to make a porch, and we had the men lay out the Foundation, and I had to buy way too many corded tools to make it the right way; strength and…</p>
<h1 id="toc239"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>What the fuck do you mean?<br/>
<span style="text-decoration: line-through;">No no no no</span>. It can’t have been that long. It can’t have been.</p>
<h4 id="toc240"><span>END SCENE.</span></h4>
</div>

<div class="script">
<h3 id="toc241"><span>ACT TWO, SCENE FOUR</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">800 words.</span></p>
<p>INT. SCHOOL - 1926.<sup class="footnoteref"><a class="footnoteref" href="javascript:;" id="footnoteref-6" onclick="WIKIDOT.page.utils.scrollToReference('footnote-6')">6</a></sup></p>
<p>The graduation is an achievement for which the sun celebrates. The students it blankets deserve it. The light is yellow, golden when it's reflected right off of the glass at the far-right of stage, an extension of the school’s edifice, which peeks over the STAGE’s right barrier.<br/>
The STAGE has expanded.</p>
<p>It is now concrete, and <em>a</em> stage has been erected at the opposite end of the STAGE. This makeshift stage’s supports are visible under the thin blue tarp which covers the particleboard. The mahogany podium atop is imposing, almost as much as the two man-sized speakers which face toward the crowd at the stage’s periphery.</p>
<p>The crowd is of a decent size, partitioned into two sides with a walkway down the middle. There are a mixture of all MOUTH-ENTITIES, with the short, fat, and the lame among those in attendance. They sweat, and the stench of figs and stone is strong, each playing off the other. We are in nature, and it is beautiful.</p>
<h1 id="toc242"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>I'm sorry I never went to your graduation. I remember when you did, you know? When you were cryin’, asking me why I hadn’t come. I couldn’t swap shifts on time. Had to work during it. Poor thing.</p>
<h1 id="toc243"><span>COMMANDER (CONT'D)</span></h1>
<p>Y'know, I didn’t care about it while I was on shift at all. I just worked and bantered with coworkers. Same as always.<sup class="footnoteref"><a class="footnoteref" href="javascript:;" id="footnoteref-7" onclick="WIKIDOT.page.utils.scrollToReference('footnote-7')">7</a></sup></p>
<h1 id="toc244"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>It didn’t matter. You’d better not worry about that.</p>
<p>In a rapid event that flows over into time immeasurable, the teachers and doctors and officials make their speeches, in clipped speech and shreek screeches; the crowd grows in intensity as half-minutes pass by, until they are a crowd of screaming lunatics, all in great agreement—and a banister is unfurled at the end of the fourth official’s speech, when they’re gesturing wildly and snapping their head to the long scream which reads “LONG HAPPY AHEAD.” in scrawled, gold-flaked lettering; the MOUTH-ENTITIES take a moment to point their tongues to it, and DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE waits, a pained expression on its face. The earpiece chirps.</p>
<h1 id="toc245"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc246"><span>(IN PRAYER)</span></h1>
<p>I’m a horrible fucking mother. Forgive me for my sins.</p>
<p>The teen-mouth-entity will now receive his awards. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE tries to speak to him over the mass. The two are equal now—it has aged over the years, and it’s begun to wrinkle, the hair now <em>dyed</em> jet-black.</p>
<h1 id="toc247"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>I wonder if it <em>is</em> best you go out there. Maybe they need you.</p>
<h1 id="toc248"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Hey.</p>
<h1 id="toc249"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>But I can’t accept that. No.</p>
<h1 id="toc250"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>How have you been? Son.</p>
<p>Haltingly, the son speaks.</p>
<h1 id="toc251"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Ah.</p>
<p>It looks down at its shoes, and he stares at the stage, waiting for the obligation to pass. It keeps trying.</p>
<h1 id="toc252"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>You know. I always liked you. Always thought you a good kid. Was always proud of you.</p>
<p>At this, the son’s head snaps up. He is angered by it, and his voice reflects this. The chirps are almost screeches in their speed.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE offers no resistance, only acceptance.</p>
<p>The boy is unsure as to whether he would have preferred this weakness over the fight he expected.</p>
<p>Tentatively, DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE approaches the SON-ENTITY. He doesn’t step away from it.</p>
<h1 id="toc253"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>I know I should have done more. I think. But it’s too late to dwell on that now, don’t you think. I just want to be here while I can.</p>
<p>The SON-ENTITY squirms. The speaker has come off the stage. Students stream onto it. He <em>should</em> be with them.</p>
<h1 id="toc254"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Wait! Wait a moment!</p>
<p>He begins ambling out of the arrangement, and walks slowly towards the stage, watching his step as though he is over a great cavern, and it follows him.</p>
<h1 id="toc255"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Can’t you hear me? Can’t you stop for a second? Goddamn you!”</p>
<h1 id="toc256"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc257"><span>(WITH GREAT HATE)</span></h1>
<p>You get what you deserve, DISPOSABLE.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE seizes him. His face is relaxed and drooping. He is gone.</p>
<h1 id="toc258"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Please, you have to say <em>something.</em> At least forgive me, for fuck’s sake!</p>
<p>He continues walking, halfway to the stage, and the sun is brilliant over the people, melting them into one under its citrus chine. It stops in its tracks, it’s racking itself in loud, choked sobs.</p>
<h1 id="toc259"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p><em><span style="color: #8c328c">“You have to forgive me, you bitch."</span></em></p>
<p>The stage takes the son-entity into its maw, filled with a thrashing mass of MOUTH-ENTITIES that trip and tilt around the crooked beams.</p>
<p>It will swallow.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE closes and opens its mouth, engulfed in panic, and moans softly.</p>
<p>The board breaks under the weight of the hundreds, and a loud snap resounds and bounds off the brick as they fall. A hole has been dug under the stage; it may go on forever.</p>
<p>Somehow, you not only see the son-entity as he falls, but feel the vertigo in your innards.</p>
<p>It is good.</p>
<h4 id="toc260"><span>END SCENE.</span></h4>
</div>

<div class="script">
<h3 id="toc261"><span>ACT TWO, SCENE FIVE</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">800 words.</span><br/>
EXT. BACKYARD. - MIDNIGHT.</p>
<p>The theater's roof is gone, revealing the night sky. The artificial light is obvious, the stage's spotlights clearly visible.</p>
<p>A swinging chair with the canopy wrenched off and placed to the side holds DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE and the toddler MOUTH-ENTITY.</p>
<p>The mouthpiece chirps.</p>
<h1 id="toc262"><span>SALVADOR</span></h1>
<p>.4 lux detected. The stars may not be visible. Recommend decamping towards ⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀⠀ if you wish to stargaze.</p>
<h1 id="toc263"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Not yet, SALVADOR. I cannot go eastward ‘till she does too.</p>
<p>She coos, her boisterous speech apparent through the language barrier. It beams with pride.</p>
<h1 id="toc264"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Yes! You’re thirsty, aren’t you?</p>
<p>She responds. It's an achievement Dad is not yet used to.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE manifests a <em>cup</em> of viscous green liquid, and she reaches for the top. It holds it out of reach for a few seconds, playing with her.</p>
<h1 id="toc265"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>You can do it girl! Come on, just a bit higher. Just…</p>
<p>It lets the baby open her head and drink from the cup.</p>
<h1 id="toc266"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Yes, like that girl. I told you you could do it, didn’t I?</p>
<p>It watches the kid for a while. The toddler watches the "sky" above, learning from it, eyes wide with wondering.</p>
<p>The WIFE-ENTITY enters the stage. She sits to DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE’s side. DISPOSABLE-ONE–TWELVE looks at its wife for a while.</p>
<h1 id="toc267"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>You’re quite rough today. Something off?</p>
<p>It squints as hard as it can and leans toward the WIFE-ENTITY.</p>
<h1 id="toc268"><span>WIFE-ENTITY</span></h1>
<p>I’ve… I feel hollow without our Son. Maybe hollow is an okay word.</p>
<h1 id="toc269"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Me too. Not as though we can do anything about it though. No, nothing at all.</p>
<p>The WIFE-ENTITY is startled, almost jumping at the reply. For a moment, it looks at DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE.</p>
<h1 id="toc270"><span>WIFE-ENTITY</span></h1>
<p>You can hear me?</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE nods. She suppresses a frown. The revelation is subsumed swiftly. The two sit in swinging silence. The baby coos intermittently.</p>
<p>A chair creaks in the distance, obfuscated by a digital compression algorithm.</p>
<h1 id="toc271"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Do you know what happened to him, DISPOSABLE? You know who I’m talking about.</p>
<h1 id="toc272"><span>COMMANDER (CONT’D)</span></h1>
<p>You know. He hasn’t been taking this well. I’ve heard <em>much</em> from him—at least, as much as I can from here. None of it’s been good.</p>
<h1 id="toc273"><span>COMMANDER (CONT’D)</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc274"><span>(WITH MUTED DISMAY)</span></h1>
<p>Anything? I beg you, Twelve, anything.</p>
<h1 id="toc275"><span>COMMANDER (CONT’D)</span></h1>
<p>If nothing else, think about Myke. Maybe you don’t like me. That’s fine. I won’t grovel for forgiveness like you do. But Myke deserves it. More than either of us.</p>
<h1 id="toc276"><span>COMMANDER (CONT’D)</span></h1>
<p>I haven’t left you. Don’t leave me.</p>
<p>He removes the earpiece and speaks quietly.</p>
<h1 id="toc277"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc278"><span>(CALMLY)</span></h1>
<p>You don’t deserve me. You don’t deserve your fucking DISPOSABLE. Let me be. Let me live.</p>
<h1 id="toc279"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc280"><span>(BEGGING)</span></h1>
<p>And how can you say that? You’re not living!</p>
<h1 id="toc281"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE:</span></h1>
<p><em>I have lived longer here than I did out there. I have children. A wife. I’ve worked, for <strong>them</strong>, years. You think <strong>I’m</strong> the one that needs to live?</em></p>
<p>The COMMANDER gasps.</p>
<h1 id="toc282"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>Holy shit. Holy shit. You <em>lived</em> during that? That whole blur?</p>
<h1 id="toc283"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc284"><span>(ASTONISHED)</span></h1>
<p>What else would I have done? It’s <em>you</em> that failed to see how I lived. How I was. I was glad to be without you for twenty years, COMMANDER.</p>
<h1 id="toc285"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>You… how could you… what?</p>
<p>At this, the WIFE-ENTITY perks.</p>
<h1 id="toc286"><span>WIFE-ENTITY</span></h1>
<p>20 years?</p>
<p>But <span style="text-decoration: line-through;">he</span> does not hear.</p>
<p>The WIFE-ENTITY clicks a bit, noticing the subdued altercation. She sees the earpiece, and her jaw shifts, opening to show her calloused tongue nervously passing through dozens of sharp teeth.</p>
<p>She tries to defuse. It doesn't work; it is beyond reconciliation now. It deserves only cauterization.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE rises from the chair and hands the kid to the WIFE-ENTITY. It paces swiftly around the STAGE, the WIFE-ENTITY’s jaw fixed upon it.</p>
<h1 id="toc287"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc288"><span>(RESENTFULLY)</span></h1>
<p>Did you just forget about me? Did you go <em>live</em>, COMMANDER? I know for a fact you <em>fucking</em> didn’t, so don’t lecture me about what I do with my time.</p>
<h1 id="toc289"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc290"><span>(PLEADING)</span></h1>
<p>What would <em><strong>he</strong></em> say about that?</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE’s pace halts for a moment, and <strong>he</strong> speaks in a louder, lower voice.</p>
<h1 id="toc291"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<h1 id="toc292"><span>(angrily)</span></h1>
<p>Don’t throw mistakes at me as though <em>you</em> didn’t make any.</p>
<h1 id="toc293"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>I want you to <em>remember where you came from!</em></p>
<h1 id="toc294"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>And what if I don’t want to? You never understand—I don’t need salvation!</p>
<p>The earpiece’s audio distorts.</p>
<h1 id="toc295"><span>SALVADOR</span></h1>
<p>Warning! Bitrate declining! 32 kilobyte HE-AAC audio. There may be loss of detail. The connection may drop.</p>
<h1 id="toc296"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>You… in this world <em>need</em> you, and they should geit aferhis long time waiting fou.</p>
<h1 id="toc297"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Tell Myke he needs to move on. That <em>I</em> think I’ve become better. That's what matters.</p>
<h1 id="toc298"><span>COMMANDER</span></h1>
<p>I’sn for the bet … chu’slaf ‘way for nothing bu’a pittance tha’wahn’ do—</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE grabs the earpiece and jams it in its pocket. It goes to the chair. A dim star emerges from the STAGE’s side, the one called the Son.</p>
<h4 id="toc299"><span>END SCENE.</span></h4>
</div>
<hr/>
<div class="blockquote">
<h3 id="toc300"><span>FURTHER INFO:</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">334 words.</span><br/>
There are many difficulties in adapting LordStonefish’s work for the stage—Mulberry has infamously discussed his challenges after abandoning a decades-long attempt at adapting the <a href="https://scp-wiki.wikidot.com/scp-3999" target="_blank">Center of Me</a>—and it may interest some of the more technical viewers to learn some of the tricks we have used in order to succeed in effects encoding where LordStonefish failed.</p>
<p>Most notable in the play is the personalization through targeted memetics recently pioneered through anlit playwrights such as M. Thulassan and Daniel Marcus. This is the largest implementation of biological markers, psychic scans, and spatial shifting this side of the anart community, and we hope that it shows through some of the scenes.</p>
<p>In particular, some of the largest cues can be found in the fourth scene of the play, where viewers are convinced that the stage changes orientation and expands, just as the book’s images do in that chapter. This effect, unfortunately, is only available for our younger patrons—not merely to protect the brain sand of some of our elderly patrons, but because the neural connections themselves have to be arranged such that the image in the brain is left unedited by the primary visual cortex, which then allows us to ontokinetically bend and spin the photons without image corruption. This process, of course, was one of the main delays that the project experienced—Stephanie couldn’t bear it if one of our beta viewers suffered because of this technique—but it has, we hope, resulted in a memetic image so sharp it’s as though it’s really happening in front of your eyes.</p>
<p>Another scene that proved difficult in visualization and construction was the final scene. The controversial 5-hour time delay that the book exacted from its readers could not be repeated in good faith by Pseudogenesis, so a compression of the events was needed. While it has resulted in a fundamentally different thing—it is not a line, but a sphere!—we believe the translation of experience to show is something our regulars will love!</p>
<p>Though only time 'ought to tell~</p>
<p>~ Vivienne Chen, Memetics Specialist</p>
</div>
<hr/>
<div class="script">
<h3 id="toc301"><span>ACT THREE, SCENE ONE.</span></h3>
<hr/>
<p><span style="font-size:smaller;">800 words.</span><br/>
INT. RESTAURANT. NEAR-NOON.</p>
<p>Blue worms wriggle about in the plate as a ray of sunlight accentuates the gold rim. DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE digs into it hungrily and stares at the two mouth-entities opposite it and its wife. They all chirp around for a bit as she scoops them into her jaws. The worms smell of roasted onion, their texture similar to a brownie’s. A current of wind pierces through the ambiance with the clarity of a clarinet and depth of a didgeridoo. In the center of the table is a little bouquet of seasoning and a menu with “Daniel’s” embossed in silver lettering.</p>
<h1 id="toc302"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>You chose quite a good place, Sir. I admit, I wasn’t sure about it, but it’s… <em>understated.</em></p>
<h1 id="toc303"><span>FATHER-ENTITY</span></h1>
<p>Yes! Only fucking reason I came over here, you know that I wouldn’t want to deal with this dumbassed line shit unless they had it toned down.</p>
<p>The FATHER-ENTITY gestures to the menu as DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE leans back.</p>
<h1 id="toc304"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Well, I wouldn’t complain about a different man’s writing system, but you’re entitled to that.</p>
<p>The WIFE-ENTITY taps on DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE’s hand. It focuses.</p>
<h1 id="toc305"><span>WIFE-ENTITY</span></h1>
<p>You… Must you be here?</p>
<h1 id="toc306"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Oh, of course! If a man wants to have dinner, he shall have it.</p>
<p>The FATHER-ENTITY snickers in assent.</p>
<p>The two mouth-entities are older, with skin gray as DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE’s patchy hair and hardened skin. The male mouth entity wears a gold ring with stars ringing around it. The female does not, and her eye bores into DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE. She is the only mouth-entity that has an eye; it is restless and oddly faceless, though what makes it so detached and lonely is unknown.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE shifts in its seat and stops eating. It takes its elbows off the table.</p>
<h1 id="toc307"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>So. It’s been quite a while since I’ve had a chance to dine with you two. How’s it gone?</p>
<p>The FATHER-ENTITY clicks a bit then continues its dining.</p>
<h1 id="toc308"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Ah. My condolences. And the Missus?</p>
<p>The mother mouth-entity begins to respond. With a gruff noise, she is silenced, and the FATHER-ENTITY answers.</p>
<h1 id="toc309"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
<p>Glad to know she’s doing well.</p>
<p>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE’s wife speaks; DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE realizes that just in time.</p>
<h1 id="toc310"><span>WIFE-ENTITY</span></h1>
<p>You know, we came here so that we could learn when you would pay your due.</p>
<p>The FATHER-ENTITY tenses, and his voice is notably lower.</p>
<h1 id="toc311"><span>DISPOSABLE-ONE-TWELVE</span></h1>
